I am happy that Nationwide Distributor got ahold of me, but the true issue was not being able to redirect my package to a FedEx location locally to pick it up after work, I understand not being able to redirect the package to a totally different address but this wasn't like that, this was just wanting it to be left at a FedEx location where I have still have to prove I am the recipient of the package to pick it up, unlike delivering the package where anyone can pretend to be the recipient and forge their signature.

< text>
It is not just the awkward location or the lack of parking that made my visit here such a negative experience.

It was THE FACT THAT I WAS NEVER GREETED AFTER STANDING THERE 5-7 MINUTES.

I could hear someone in the back but I could not see them. I told myself they were busy and to be understandin and patient so I waited another few minutes and nothing.

I called out and nothing then after a few more minutes someone appeared. She made it very clear she was not happy to take my order she seemed extremely upset that I had come in to disturb her.

When she finally asked "what do you want?" I just turned and walked away. I did not place an order.

Service is only half the reason you choose a pizza place GOOD SERVICE is the other half which only adds to the experience and ENJOYMENT of your pizza.

I never had a chance to experience the Pizza but if the SERVICE, ATTITUDE AND MANNER IN WHICH I WAS TREATED AND GREETED is a reflection of the QUALITY of the pizza I did not miss a thing.

My son was still waiting at home for pizza and I did not want to disappoint him so I am so happy I drove down the street to Little Caesar's Pizza where I was greeted with a cheerful smile the moment I walked in. The young man was polite, friendly and cheerful.

I placed my order and within seconds I was out the door with my son's hot pizza and a smile.

I have no future plans, intentions or interest to visit Papa John's Pizza that kind of service, attitude and treatment looked and felt to be written in stone.

Sincerely,
Rebecca Velasquez< /text>

< Review>
“Beyond good ... VERY GOOD ❣️ Both the food and service (our waiter, Daniel was the epitome of gentle-manliness) were spectacular. The revelations began with the delightfully tasty Antipasto; we were impressed that each bite blossomed with flavor as we dwelled on each morsel.  Even the bread was fresh and tasty without garnishment; but as a vehicle for the cheeses and everything on the plate, the combinations were wonderful. EVERYTHING on the antipasti plate was full flavored and distinctive... did you hear that (?!) “full flavored and distinctive”, even the dried pear tasted like a full flavored dried pear!  Likewise for the rest of the plate.  Our main courses were likewise delicious: the meatballs were cooked medium and deliciously juicy and the accompanying al dente pasta was perfectly flavored with a well seasoned and thick tomato sauce that didn’t run — imagine that with distinctive flavors.  My wife’s scallops were excellent as well.  In closing, make reservations and get ready for gastronomic delights and thoughtful service.  My only criticism is that the Men’s’ Room should have a lighted light switch, please; the urgency grew in anticipation too long.</Review>

< Text>
If you are seriously looking to dine Italian, take a few moments to read this review.  Cafe Luna is a hidden gem!  Ambrosia!  First, they nailed it on the ambience.  Second, and most important, Chef Marcos could be straight out of Pisa, Italy with his culinary skills (we have dined in six cities in Italy).  You can create your own dish!  My husband ordered capellini with a very specific and flavorful scampi, and the pasta was exactly as requested - al dente - such a refreshing change from other restaurants serving premade mush.  I ordered a juicy sea bass with blood orange reduction (Chef Marcos likes to incorporate what is in season) and the creamiest risotto ever!  We were raising our wine glass to evety bite. Their salads are anything but boring (their Ceaser includes toasted pine nuts and capers with a fresh, homemade dressing).  Their house salad includes artichokes and Kalamata olives.  The service is very friendly, professional,  knowlegable and accommodating.  You really must experience Cafe Luna for yourself.  It is now our "Go To" whenever we crave Italian cuisine.</Text>

<rate>3<//rate><Review>This place was highly recommended by the management staff of the Marriotts hotel across the parking lot where I've been staying for business the past 3 weeks. After trying just about everywhere at San Diego's downtown dining scene (love those Gaslamp joints) I decided to give it a rest tonight.
I took the waiter's suggestion and ordered tonigh's house special. I know, I should have listened to Mario B. And never order the "house special". So here it goes....

The soup was good. Lobster bisque with shrimp. Very creamy and served at the right temperature.
The rib eye is average at best. It was tender (It was very thin and I did not use the steak knife). It was drowned in some kind of sauce. Could not pin point what the sauce is based on.
The crab cake that topped the steak was bland, Joe's Crab Shack quality at best.
The bonus "bone marrow bread pudding" is more like a Pilsburry biscuit drenched in the sauce that covered the steak.
The mash potatoe... well ..... mash potatoe.
The Italian broccoli was cold.
The other thing that is good was the bread.... warm and soft. That dip..... what it that?

The bill was $44 and change. I was just chock it up as lesson.learned and go back to my room and go to bed but then come the manager. She kept asking me how was the meal. I told her that it was alright but we just would not take that as the answer. So she pushed hoping to get the word "great" out of me. It did not work so I came clean and told her what I really thought about the meal. And now this review.
She did took $5 off the tab but I refused to accept the discount and add it to the waiter's tip for an even $50.

Here is my suggestion to that manager if she happens to run across this writing.....If the guy is reluctant to tell you about the quality of your food..... let him go. At least he is not complaining. Just because you got a few good ratings from other diners does not make your food great. Take the "food is OK" as a complement and be happy with that. It is an equivalent to a Michelin 1 star (out of most possible 3).
Not everyone complaint to get a free meal. If you are not willing to eat the whole tab then don't offer to give a guy $5 discount on a $35 steak. It is insulting to me to accept the $5 because I'm not happy with the food. BTW. At $35 diners expect a lot for that steak. You are now in the league with the joints down at Gaslamp district for that price.
Your clientele are pretty much the Olive Garden, Claim Jumper crowd. This is why you got good ratings, don't let that go over your head. You should have taken my "its OK" and be happy with that.</Review>< pics>
None</pics>

<Text>I recently adopted a dog from here. I have no issues with the staff at all, they were very friendly and welcoming.

The one reason I'm not giving them five stars is due to the pandemic regulations on the adoptions. I totally get why one person with a mask at a time in the facility is a must and that the health of the employees is very important. But I don't quite get why the adoption process has become more difficult.

You can't walk through the facility and look at the dogs they have on your visit. You have to go to the website and look at the list of dogs they have, of which isn't updated for a few days sometimes, and call to make an appointment with one specific dog.

Then at the appointment, you can't spend time with the dog to get a read on it's personality. You can only look at it through a glass door, and after that you have to decide whether or not you want to put the adoption fee down.

If you do decide to put money down, the dog gets fixed a few days later and then you're able to go in a room and spend time with them. If by that visit you decide you don't think that dog is a good fit for you, you can choose to get a refund but that refund is a check sent in the mail from the county and can take a week or two to get to you. This refund process was explained to me by one of the staff.

I just really wish I would have been able to look at all the dogs on the appointment day to make the adoption process a little bit smoother.

Aside from that one bump in the road, my experience was generally positive. I am very happy with my new buddy. Animal services offers a free exam (at select clinics) up to 14 days after adoption, which is great.<//Text>< Rate>
